# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Your Task

Envoy discovers its various dynamic resources via the filesystem or by\\n7: querying one or more management servers. Collectively, these discovery\\n8: services and their corresponding APIs are referred to as ``xDS``.\\n9: Resources are requested via ``subscriptions``, by specifying a filesystem\\n10: path to watch, initiating gRPC streams, or polling a REST-JSON URL. The\\n11: latter two methods involve sending requests with a :ref:`DiscoveryRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.discovery.v3.DiscoveryRequest>`\\n12: proto payload. Resources are delivered in a\\n13: :ref:`DiscoveryResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.discovery.v3.DiscoveryResponse>`\\n14: proto payload in all methods. In various requests from\\n38: Envoy and responses by the management server, the resource type URL is stated.\\n39: \",\"endLine\":39,\"startLine\":36}],\"file\":\"docs/root/api-docs/xds_protocol.rst\",\"repo\":\"github.com/envoyproxy/envoy\",\"type\":\"file\",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/-/blob/docs/root/api-docs/xds_protocol.rst\"},{\"chunks\":[{\"content\":\"9: **tl;dr**: xDS can use the filesystem, REST or gRPC. gRPC xDS comes in four flavors.\\n10: However, Envoy code uses all of that via the same `Subscription` interface.\\n11: If you are an Envoy developer with your hands on a valid `Subscription` object,\\n12: you can mostly forget the filesystem/REST/gRPC distinction, and you can\\n13: \",\"endLine\":13,\"startLine\":9},{\"content\":\"23: The key components are:\\n24: * `GrpcMuxImpl` which manages the xDS transport and multiplexing one or more subscriptions on a\\n25:   single gRPC stream. The muxer is responsible for managing the wire level concerns via\\n26:   `GrpcStream`, while also tracking subscription state and watchers for updates. Multiple resource\\n27:   type URLs may be managed by a single muxer. For non-ADS, this will always be one stream per\\n28:   subscription, whereas for ADS, multiple subscriptions will be multiplexed on a single stream.\\n29: * `SubscriptionState` tracks subscription state for a single resource type URL.\\n30: * `WatchMap` tracks all the subscribers for a given resource type.\\n31: * Each Envoy subsystem, e.g. LDS, CDS, etc. has a `GrpcSubscriptionImpl` that points at a `GrpcMuxImpl`.\\n32: \\n33: The above components are responsible for subscriptions, watches, muxing and stream management.\\n34: Caching is not currently a centralized service, and is instead delegated to per-resource type\\n35: modules such as `RdsRouteConfigProviderImpl`.\\n36: ... [chunk truncated]\",\"endLine\":36,\"startLine\":23},{\"content\":\"36: \\n37: Note that there can be multiple active gRPC subscriptions for a single resource type. This concept\\n38: is called \\\"resource watches\\\". If one EDS subscription subscribes to X and Y, and another subscribes\\n39: to Y and Z, the underlying subscription logic will maintain a subscription to the union: X Y and Z.\\n40: Updates to X will be delivered to the first object, Y to both, Z to the second. \",\"endLine\":41,\"startLine\":36}],\"file\":\"source/docs/xds.md\",\"repo\":\"github.com/envoyproxy/envoy\",\"type\":\"file\",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/-/blob/source/docs/xds.md\"},{\"chunks\":[{\"content\":\"1: pools. DetectorConfig: Configuration parameters for ejection thresholds and detection criteria\\n  - EventLoggerImpl: Logs outlier detection events\\n\\nThe integration with health checking occurs through the putResult() method which receives health check outcomes and updates outlier detection statistics. The outlier detection system tracks consecutive failures, success rates, and can uneject hosts based on successful active health checks (via successful_active_health_check_uneject_host_ configuration).\\n\\n## Core Upstream Infrastructure\\n\\nSupporting infrastructure files:\\n- **source/common/upstream/upstream_impl.h/cc**: ClusterImplBase that owns and manages the health checker, delegates health check results to outlier detection, and tracks host health state.\\n- **source/common/upstream/host_utility.h/cc**: Utility functions for health flag management and serialization.\\n\\n## Architecture Flow\\n\\nThe complete flow is: CDS subscription -> cluster updates -> cluster manager adds/updates clusters -> health checker factory creates health checker instances -> health checker starts Active Health Check Sessions with interval timers -> health check results flow to outlier detection -> outlier detection ejects/unejects hosts based on configurable thresholds and can be influenced by active health check successes.\"\n}\n",

Implements the ActiveHealthCheckSession class with interval timer and timeout timer management, handles health transitions, and manages callbacks.\\n\\n**Protocol-Specific Health Checkers:**\\n- **source/extensions/health_checkers/http/health_checker_impl.h/cc**: HTTP health check implementation (HttpHealthCheckerImpl) with HTTP request/response handling.\\n- **source/extensions/health_checkers/tcp/health_checker_impl.h/cc**: TCP health check implementation (TcpHealthCheckerImpl) with TCP connect verification.\\n- **source/extensions/health_checkers/grpc/health_checker_impl.h/cc**: gRPC health check implementation (GrpcHealthCheckerImpl) using the gRPC health check protocol.\\n- **source/extensions/health_checkers/redis/config.h/cc**: Redis health check implementation.\\n- **source/extensions/health_checkers/thrift/config.h/cc**: Thrift health check implementation.\\n\\n**Health Check Infrastructure:**\\n- **source/common/upstream/health_checker_impl.h/cc**: Factory (HealthCheckerFactory) and utility functions for creating health checker instances.\\n- **source/common/upstream/health_checker_event_logger.h/cc**: Event logging for health check events.\\n- **source/common/upstream/health_discovery_service.h/cc**: Health Discovery Service (HDS) that receives cluster health configurations from a management server.\\n\\n## Outlier Detection Integration\\n\\nThe outlier detection mechanism is implemented in:\\n- **source/common/upstream/outlier_detection_impl.h/cc**: Core outlier detection implementation including:\\n  - DetectorImpl: Main detector class that runs periodic checks (onIntervalTimer) to identify unhealthy hosts based on success rates, consecutive errors, etc.\\n  - DetectorHostMonitorImpl: Per-host monitor that tracks failure statistics and ejects/unejects hosts based on configured thresholds\\n  - DetectorConfig: Configuration parameters for ejection thresholds and detection criteria\\n  - EventLoggerImpl: Logs outlier detection events\\n\\nThe integration with health checking occurs through the putResult() method which receives health check outcomes and updates outlier detection statistics. The outlier detection system tracks consecutive failures, success rates, and can uneject hosts based on successful active health checks (via successful_active_health_check_uneject_host_ configuration).\\n\\n## Core Upstream Infrastructure\\n\\nSupporting infrastructure files:\\n- **source/common/upstream/upstream_impl.h/cc**: ClusterImplBase that owns and manages the health checker, delegates health check results to outlier detection, and tracks host health state.\\n- **source/common/upstream/host_utility.h/cc**: Utility functions for health flag management and serialization.\\n\\n## Architecture Flow\\n\\nThe complete flow is: CDS subscription -> cluster updates -> cluster manager adds/updates clusters -> health checker factory creates health checker instances -> health checker starts Active Health Check Sessions with interval timers -> health check results flow to outlier detection -> outlier detection ejects/unejects hosts based on configurable thresholds and can be influenced by active health check successes.\"\n}\n",
